Killing the Fishmonger 201

Xiao En was so angry that his face turned green; Li Jun was extremely indignant and stepped forward to persuade Zhang San; Gui Ying was so frightened that she left crying. Huang San pointed at his own nose and said, "Do you know who I am?" and then punched Li Jun in the head.

Novel

Ramblings in Siam (8) 202

— Yimin

Last year can be said to have been a disastrous year for the overseas Chinese in Siam. Since the Kuomintang government came to power in that country, there have been various amendments to immigration regulations (those who are illiterate cannot enter, and those under twenty years old cannot leave), increases in entry taxes (previously, going to Siam only required an entry tax of 15 Siamese baht per person, but now it has been increased to 100 Siamese baht; the cost of a return Siamese passport has also increased from 5 yuan to 20 yuan); the adoption of Siamese bookkeeping (from banks to grocery stores, all must use Siamese books for the government to check at any time); the imposition of various harsh taxes (in addition to the original poll tax, there are also income taxes, remittance taxes, old goods taxes, and heavy taxes on daily necessities such as matches); and the implementation of so-called compulsory education (explained in the next section). Various harsh laws were implemented one after another last year. In addition, the world was in recession, and evil demons broke into Siam, causing several rice mills and sawmills to close down due to stagnant sales. Many shops, unable to repay their debts, recklessly set fires themselves in order to evade debt, and the number of matchmakers also increased day by day. These phenomena illustrate that the golden age of the overseas Chinese in Siam has become a thing of the past.

Overseas Chinese have been running schools in Siam for more than twenty years. There are more than one hundred primary schools in total (excluding private schools), with four or five thousand students. Middle schools have only been established in the last two or three years, including schools such as Overseas Chinese, China, Nanyang, Xinmin, and Chongbao, but they only offer junior high school, and the number of middle school students is also very small, probably less than 500. If we assume that school-age children account for 200,000 of the 3 million overseas Chinese, then less than one-fifth are educated, and the age of the students is mostly over the school age. A primary school graduate is usually 18 or 19 years old, so the underdevelopment of overseas Chinese education in Siam is evident here.

Film Special

Republic of China, 23rd Year, April 10th, Tuesday

Section Sereon Pao Shun The

On "Evaluation of The Flame" and Others 203

— Ling He

When I happened to read Mr. Mu Tian's "Evaluation of The Flame," I couldn't help but feel a little perplexed. This is because he went to see it not only under the influence of a long period of advertising promotion but also because he "saw an overly high evaluation in the Film Special," resulting in him "going excitedly and returning disappointed." Therefore, I cannot help but ask myself, did I really deceive this "progressive poet"? Otherwise, the poet would only be able to write poetry and still "not understand the reason" for the movie.

The criticism of "The Flame" was written by me. Because I have to be responsible to the readers, I really wanted to write something to tell the readers and answer Mr. Mu Tian at that time. But later I believed that the article was not that wrong after all, and I did not require every audience of "The Flame" to have exactly the same opinion as mine (which of course is also impossible). So why waste time and ink?

But things are often not as simple as we imagine. After reading several large evening newspapers for several days in a row, it seemed like I had to say something. This is the motivation for me to write this article.

Regarding "The Flame," in fact, I definitely don't want to defend the playwright, but from the playwright's choice of subject matter to processing, he has to take into account the current bad environment and say what we want to say in a roundabout way. This point, apart from those who are deliberately spokespersons for the powerful or gentlemen who are helping to cruelly attack Chinese movies, should indeed sympathize with the playwright's hard work and give some forgiveness; even if he has small errors in technology. That's right, under the current environment, the director has to avoid the important and take the light, and make many unnecessary articles outside the theme (such as the depiction of Ah Zhen's vanity), and even change the flames of the landlord's dancing burning the thatched shed to Ah Zhen's carelessness. Is it worth the poet to scold so harshly for things like this? At the same time, it is also absolutely true that we have to emphasize the demand for reality, there is no problem with this. For example, we ask the author of "Wind" to pay attention to 100% reality in the future, but when we know that it has undergone some unreasonable cutting, we cannot help but sympathize with the author's hard work. However, Mr. Mu Tian said that "Fallen Flowers" and "Cage" are all undesirable "decadent images," which is inevitably an irrational request. As for saying that the "watery eyes," "small bridges and flowing water," and "dense green trees" all make the poet look down on them; even to explain that the fire brigade is at the corner of Yuyuan Road and Difeng Road, and the villa is in Jiangwan, etc., it can only make people laugh. The former certainly should not exaggerate the natural scenery of the countryside too much and destroy the film's emotions, which can only be said to be the director's inability to understand further, but we definitely do not say that "small bridges" should not have "flowing water" and "green trees" should not have "dense shade," which is 100% reality. As for the latter, more people don't believe that explaining that the fire brigade is in front of Mr. Mu Tian's house or the villa is behind his house is "conceptual" and "not fictional."

In Mr. Mu Tian's consecutive articles, he repeatedly mentioned the demand for reality in movies, as mentioned above, we can know how he explains reality. However, if we observe further, he is just using reality as an excuse, and is actually destroying more meaningful Chinese movies, and exhausting his responsibility to "help out," then we will not know how to appreciate the "artistic" intentions of this "progressive poet." As for saying that the insurance company in "The Flame" is intentionally "preaching for imperialism" and that the workers in "Fragrant Grass Beauty" should speak in a mess, making the entire surface incoherent and clueless, that is the unfathomable poet's opinion.

(To be continued)

Film Review of "Evidence of Guilt" 204

— Luo Ping

Sleepers East丨Great Shanghai丨

Detective films, like Gangster films, are outdated. Although detective films have attracted the psychology of many petty citizen audiences.

Petty citizens feel the daily life is annoying, dull, and ordinary, they need excitement, so detective films, like detective novels, are loved by petty citizens.

This "Evidence of Guilt" is moved from a novel to the screen.

Ordinary detective films always tell us how cruel, how vicious, and how unforgivable the criminals are, and on the other hand, they tell us how brave, how intelligent, and how wise the detectives are, making people admire them.

However, in "Evidence of Guilt," the insidiousness and treachery of the citizens are objectively exposed. This is the commendable part of "Evidence of Guilt," although this is not the theme, and the focus is still on "love."

Moreover, "Evidence of Guilt" is also different from other detective films. Ordinary detective films use a tortuous and bizarre structure, unexpected horror, and a tense atmosphere to grab the audience's emotions. But in this "Evidence of Guilt," the appearance of the murderer and how the tragedy occurred are clearly explained first. This is the difference between "Evidence of Guilt" and other detective films, and it is also the reason why "Evidence of Guilt" cannot grab the audience's emotions.

Therefore, "Evidence of Guilt" is a mediocre detective film. In terms of performance, it is a complete failure. Lengthy dialogues, tedious stories, and a dull atmosphere, all of this completely fails to grab and tense up the audience's emotions. And here, there are also inevitable coincidences and forced combinations like other detective films, such as Gai Ander killing Lai Chi, and coincidentally seeing Wen Hua killing Lai Chi, etc. are far-fetched places.

The director's handling is also not good, but that Wen Qi Poxun performed satisfactorily.

Review of "The Magic of Women" 205

— Xun Zhi

"The Women in His Life"

丨Cathay丨

The story goes like this. A lawyer accepts a defense case for a murder suspect. The murdered person is a middle-aged woman, and the suspect is the woman's husband. Coincidentally, the murdered woman happens to be the lawyer who is now defending the suspect's former lover. They had a love affair before, and later the woman disappeared, and the man, until the day of the crime, still regarded her as a lover he thought about day and night.

Such a subject matter, from the point of view of farce, is a good story. As long as the characters' personalities and environmental configurations are appropriate, perhaps a fairly powerful film can be produced.

However, what we see on the screen now is completely opposite to what we expected. The personality of the protagonist lawyer is described as very vague and contradictory. When he appears on stage, he is a playboy. His profession seems to be not handling cases but just socializing with women. Under such an atmosphere, once a former lover is killed, he will be shocked, grieved, and even driven to madness, which is no longer believable.

In addition, in this film, the audience's sympathy is mostly biased towards the suspect and his daughter, so the lawyer's "deep affection" and the conflict between his profession and emotions completely become an unnoticed existence. The psychological description from after his madness until he designs to solve the case cannot be understood and sympathized with by the audience. Therefore, the shortcoming of the play can be said to be the failure to grasp the center of the story and the inability to distinguish the levels of the theme and the sidelines, the inability to strengthen the theme, and the inability to control the audience's emotions, which is the weakness of the film's director.

In "The Fugitive," we learned that the so-called law is a tool that can be stretched and changed arbitrarily by a few people, and in this "Magic of Women," perhaps it is not the original intention of the producers, but it clearly tells us that the law is something close to a game. Regardless of the life and death of others, in addition to making money and gaining fame, there are probably quite a few who do not regard the case as their responsibility as "spokespersons for justice." If we say that the most worthwhile thing to watch in this film is that its authenticity lies in exposing the lives and social functions of this kind of people, of course, this is not the result expected by the producers.

As mentioned above, this film already has major shortcomings in terms of playwriting, and the disorder of the techniques is secondary. In the second half, because the emphasis is on detective fun and the places that should be tense, it is even more fragmented and trivial. This is a work that lowers MGM's standard.

After entering, the usual Happy Ending can be spared criticism, but the wedding in the last group can really be said to be an example of the film's producers not having seriousness towards art.

Celebrities' Habits and Hobbies 206

— Donglin

Clark Gable has the habit of going to the barbershop once a day. It's not for fashion, but because recently too many white hairs have grown.

John Barrymore does not use scissors to cut his nails, he carefully bites them off with his teeth.

Constance Bennett has a hobby of collecting pajamas. It is said that she now has seventeen sets of silk pajamas.

William Rogers often seems to be chewing on something in his mouth. People thought he was probably chewing on chewing gum, but later they found out that he was actually chewing on rubber bands (a common small rubber band for wrapping things).

Neil Hamilton is a very fond of cars, and he is also a clean person, changing his pants at least three times a day.

Joe Brown has never smoked since he was born, and maybe he will never smoke in the future!

Mae West will drive around to look for houses whenever she has time. She will run into any house with a "for rent" sign, look at it clearly, and the intention is unknown to us.

Silver Flowers 207

— Ming

The new film "X-Ray" has been extremely busy since it started filming. It is said that the interior and exterior scenes are being carried out together. Yesterday, the interior scenes of the Guanghua Silk Weaving Company were filmed. The scene was very complicated, and under the hard instructions of director Shen Tiansheng, the result was very satisfactory. The company is committed to creating new talents, so the personnel in "X-Ray" are all newcomers. The male leads of the drama are Xiao Gang and Lu Jianying, and the female lead is Ms. Chen Qiuyin, all of whom are new silver screen talents with excellent learning.

"Little Women" Premieres Tomorrow - A Great Contribution from the Great Shanghai Theater 208

"Little Women" is an important masterpiece in literature. It inspires good impressions in many ways. Now the entire plot of this book has been filmed into a movie, which will premiere at the Great Shanghai Theater on Xizang Road and Nanjing Road tomorrow. The film was produced by RKO Pictures, and the editing techniques and compilation guidelines are top-notch, with many new contributions. The protagonist is Kathleen Hepburn, the second Garbo, who gave her full performance. Because of her hard work in this film, she won the Academy's Best Honor and leaped to become the champion of the top ten famous film elections last year. The director is George Cukor, the giant of "Gone with the Wind" and "Dinner at Eight". These two all-rounders together undoubtedly aroused the great attention of the general audience.

Records of War Drums and Sword Shadows (Nana) (4) 209

— Yin Ming

One day, as they were strolling in the garden, Nana suddenly stopped and pulled up something with many leaves. She exclaimed in surprise, "Oh! So this is a radish! I always thought it grew on carts!" This made George laugh heartily, and he embraced her. Nana, in his arms, sighed happily. She said, "I love this place. I hope you do too." George said, "Of course, I do. From here, I can see your window." He pointed to a window and asked, "Is that your room?" Nana said, "Yes. That room is beautiful, but it feels too big for a woman! It makes one feel strangely lonely." George said, "That window is only three feet from the ground. Aren't you afraid sleeping alone?" Nana widened her eyes and asked, "Afraid of what?" "Well... aren't you afraid of someone who fears nothing?" Nana said, "There are no such reckless people nearby." George said, "But there is indeed a madman..." As he said this, he embraced her and kissed her passionately. Nana said coyly, "Darling, be careful someone sees us." George said, "Besides Soi, Mimi, and Keding, there's no one else around. Don't they already understand our situation?" At that moment, Soi, Mimi, Keding, and the others were also discussing the two of them. Soi, in her worldly-wise and prescient tone, said to Keding, "Let them be. If a man and a woman will make love even in a vegetable garden, then it's definitely incurable!"

After four weeks like this, his older brother, Antley, had already heard rumors about his brother and Nana. One morning, his older brother was in the house using a telescope to look at the house next door. The place he was looking at was that window, three feet from the ground. After looking for a while, he put down the telescope and waited for his brother to return. After a while, his brother indeed returned, but he didn't enter through the main door; instead, he jumped in through the window. He jumped in and was startled to see his brother with a stern face. Antley coldly said to his brother, "You're really early. I'm afraid you've used this window more than once, haven't you?" George quickly tried to cover up, "I went out for a walk this morning, and because I didn't want to disturb the family, I didn't go through the main door." Antley glared at his brother and said, "There are several ways to disturb the family. George, our family is a famous family. I hope you can respect it." George said, "I don't think I've done anything to disrespect the family's reputation." Antley said angrily, "I've known about this woman for a long time. You... she..." George interrupted, "Slow down, Antley. I love that woman. That's all there is to it. I love her, and I'm going to marry her soon." "Marry? You and her?" George said, "That's right. Please change your tone." "You fool! You're a child!" Antley touched his forehead, appearing utterly disappointed. Then, suddenly, his expression changed, becoming that of a military officer addressing a subordinate. (To be continued)
